Mainly involves removing\n                invalid fields, or renaming fields as necessary.\n                \"\"\"\n                q_tree = luqum_parser(work_query)\n\n                for node, parents in luqum_traverse(q_tree):\n                    if isinstance(node, luqum.tree.SearchField) and node.name != '*':\n                        new_name = convert_work_field_to_edition_field(node.name)\n                        if new_name:\n                            parent = parents[-1] if parents else None\n                            # Prefixing with + makes the field mandatory\n                            if isinstance(\n                                parent, (luqum.tree.Not, luqum.tree.Prohibit)\n                            ):\n                                node.name = new_name\n                            else:\n                                node.name = f'+{new_name}'\n                        else:\n                            try:\n                                luqum_remove_child(node, parents)\n                            except EmptyTreeError:\n                                # Deleted the whole tree! Nothing left\n                                return ''\n\n                return str(q_tree)\n\n            # Move over all fq parameters that can be applied to editions.\n            # These are generally used to handle facets.\n            editions_fq = ['type:edition']\n            for param_name, param_value in params:\n                if param_name != 'fq' or param_value.startswith('type:'):\n                    continue\n                field_name, field_val = param_value.split(':', 1)\n                ed_field = convert_work_field_to_edition_field(field_name)\n                if ed_field:\n                    editions_fq.append(f'{ed_field}:{field_val}')\n            for fq in editions_fq:\n                params.append(('editions.fq', fq))\n\n            user_lang = convert_iso_to_marc(web.ctx.lang or 'en') or 'eng'\n\n            ed_q = convert_work_query_to_edition_query(str(work_q_tree))\n            full_ed_query = '({{!edismax bq=\"{bq}\" v=\"{v}\" qf=\"{qf}\"}})'.format(\n                # See qf in work_query\n                qf='text title^4',\n                # Because we include the edition query inside the v=\"...\" part,\n                # we need to escape quotes. Also note that if there is no\n                # edition query (because no fields in the user's work query apply),\n                # we use the special value *:* to match everything, but still get\n                # boosting.\n                v=ed_q.replace('\"', '\\\\\"') or '*:*',\n                # bq (boost query): Boost which edition is promoted to the top\n                bq=' '.join(\n                    (\n                        f'language:{user_lang}^40',\n                        'ebook_access:public^10',\n                        'ebook_access:borrowable^8',\n                        'ebook_access:printdisabled^2',\n                        'cover_i:*^2',\n                    )\n                ),\n            )\n\n        if ed_q or len(editions_fq) > 1:\n            # The elements in _this_ edition query should cause works not to\n            # match _at all_ if matching editions are not found\n            if ed_q:\n                params.append(('edQuery', full_ed_query))\n            else:\n                params.append(('edQuery', '*:*'))\n            q = ' '.join(\n                (\n                    f'+{full_work_query}',\n                    # This is using the special parent query syntax to, on top of\n                    # the user's `full_work_query`, also only find works which have\n                    # editions matching the edition query.\n                    # Also include edition-less works (i.e. edition_count:0)\n                    '+(_query_:\"{!parent which=type:work v=$edQuery filters=$editions.fq}\" OR edition_count:0)',\n                )\n            )\n            params.append(('q', q))\n            edition_fields = {\n                f.split('.', 1)[1] for f in solr_fields if f.startswith('editions.')\n            }\n            if not edition_fields:\n                edition_fields = solr_fields - {'editions:[subquery]'}\n            # The elements in _this_ edition query will match but not affect\n            # whether the work appears in search results\n            params.append(\n                (\n                    'editions.q',\n                    # Here we use the special terms parser to only filter the\n                    # editions for a given, already matching work '_root_' node.\n                    f'({{!terms f=_root_ v=$row.key}}) AND {full_ed_query}',\n                )\n            )\n            params.append(('editions.rows', 1))\n            params.append(('editions.fl', ','.join(edition_fields)))\n        else:\n            params.append(('q', full_work_query))\n\n    if sort:\n        params.append(('sort', process_sort(sort)))\n\n    url = f'{solr_select_url}?{urlencode(params)}'\n\n    response = If it doesn't contain a /lists/ key, then\n    return the query, unchanged, exactly as it entered the\n    function. If it does contain a lists key, then use the pagination\n    information to fetch the right block of keys from the\n    lists_editions and lists_works API and then feed these editions resulting work\n    keys into solr with the form key:(OL123W, OL234W). This way, we\n    can use the solr API to fetch list works and render them in\n    carousels in the right format.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def cached_get_list_book_keys(key, offset, limit):\n        # make cacheable\n        if 'env' not in web.ctx:\n            delegate.fakeload()\n        lst = web.ctx.site.get(key)\n        return lst.get_book_keys(offset=offset, limit=limit)\n\n    if '/lists/' in q:\n        # we're making an assumption that q is just a list key\n        book_keys = cache.memcache_memoize(\n            cached_get_list_book_keys, \"search.list_books_query\", timeout=5 * 60\n        )(q, offset, limit)\n\n        q = f\"key:({' OR '.join(book_keys)})\"\n\n        # We've applied the offset to fetching get_list_editions to\n        # produce the right set of discrete work IDs. affect the rest of the query until another field is hit.\n   136→\n   137→    Here are some examples.               # copy it along to the write space to avoid things smashing\n                # together\n                field = sf.head + field\n\n            # We will be moving left to right, so we field\n                + escaped_query[sf.pos + len(field) - 1 + offset :]\n            )\n            offset += 1\n    return escaped_query\n\n\ndef fully_escape_query(query: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Try to convert a query to basically a plain lucene string.\n\n    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo')\n    'title\\\\\\\\:foo'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo bar')\n    'title\\\\\\\\:foo bar'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('title:foo (bar baz:boo)')\n    'title\\\\\\\\:foo \\\\\\\\(bar baz\\\\\\\\:boo\\\\\\\\)'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('x:[A TO Z}')\n    'x\\\\\\\\:\\\\\\\\[A TO Z\\\\\\\\}'\n    >>> fully_escape_query('foo AND bar')\n    'foo and bar'\n    \"\"\"\n    escaped = query\n    # Escape special characters\n    escaped = re.sub(r'[\\[\\]\\(\\)\\{\\}:\"-+?~^/\\\\,]', r'\\\\\\g<0>', escaped)\n    # Remove boolean operators by making them lowercase\n    escaped = re.sub(r'AND|OR|NOT', lambda _1: _1.group(0).lower(), escaped)\n    return escaped\n\n\ndef luqum_parser(query: str) -> Item:\n    \"\"\"\n    Parses a lucene-like query, with the special binding rules of Open Library.\n\n    In our queries, unlike native solr/lucene, field names are greedy, and\n    affect the rest of the query until another field is hit.\n\n    Here are some examples. The first query is the native solr/lucene\n    parsing. The second is the parsing we want.\n\n    Query : title:foo bar\n    Lucene: (title:foo) bar\n    OL    : (title:foo bar)\n\n    Query : title:foo OR bar AND author:blah\n    Lucene: (title:foo) OR (bar) AND (author:blah)\n    OL    : (title:foo OR bar) AND (author:blah)\n\n    This requires an annoying amount of manipulation of the default\n    Luqum parser, unfortunately.\n\n    Also, OL queries allow spaces after fields.\n    \"\"\"\n    tree = parser.parse(query)\n\n    def find_next_word(item: Item) -> Optional[tuple[Word, Optional[BaseOperation]]]:\n        if isinstance(item, Word):\n            return item, None\n        elif isinstance(item, BaseOperation) and isinstance(item.children[0], Word):\n            return item.children[0], item\n        else:\n            return None\n\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, BaseOperation):\n            # if any of the children are SearchField followed by one or more words,\n            # we bundle them together\n            last_sf: SearchField = None\n            to_rem = []\n            for child in node.children:\n                if isinstance(child, SearchField) and isinstance(child.expr, Word):\n                    last_sf = child\n                elif last_sf and (next_word := find_next_word(child)):\n                    word, parent_op = next_word\n                    # Add it over\n                    if not isinstance(last_sf.expr, Group):\n                        last_sf.expr = Group(type(node)(last_sf.expr, word))\n                        last_sf.expr.tail = word.tail\n                        word.tail = ''\n                    else:\n                        last_sf.expr.expr.children[-1].tail = last_sf.expr.tail\n                        last_sf.expr.expr.children += (word,)\n                        last_sf.expr.tail = word.tail\n                        word.tail = ''\n                    if parent_op:\n                        # A query like: 'title:foo blah OR author:bar\n                        # Lucene parses as: (title:foo) ? (blah OR author:bar)\n                        # We want         : (title:foo ? blah) OR (author:bar)\n                        node.op = parent_op.op\n                        node.children += (*parent_op.children[1:],)\n                    to_rem.append(child)\n                else:\n                    last_sf = None\n            if len(to_rem) == len(node.children) - 1:\n                # We only have the searchfield left!\n                if parents:\n                    # Move the head to the next element\n                    last_sf.head = node.head\n                    parents[-1].children = tuple(\n                        child if child is not node else last_sf\n                        for child in parents[-1].children\n                    )\n                else:\n                    tree = last_sf\n                    break\n            else:\n                node.children = tuple(\n                    child for child in node.children if child not in to_rem\n                )\n\n    # Remove spaces before field names\n    for node, parents in luqum_traverse(tree):\n        if isinstance(node, SearchField):\n            node.expr.head = ''\n\n    return tree\n\n\ndef query_dict_to_str(\n    escaped: dict | None = None,\n    unescaped: dict | None = None,\n    op: Literal['AND', 'OR', ''] = '',\n) -> str:\n    \"\"\"\n    Converts a query dict to a search query.\n\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo'})\n    'title:(foo)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'})\n    'title:(foo bar)  author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo bar', 'author': 'bar'}, op='OR')\n    'title:(foo bar) OR author:(bar)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'foo ? to escape'})\n    'title:(foo \\\\\\\\? to escape)'\n    >>> query_dict_to_str({'title': 'YES AND'})\n    'title:(YES and)'\n    \"\"\"\n    result = ''\n    if escaped:\n        result += f' {op} '.join(\n            f'{k}:({fully_escape_query(v)})' for k, v in escaped.items()\n        )\n    if unescaped:\n        if result:\n            result += f' {op} '\n        result += f' {op} '.join(f'{k}:{v}' for k, v in unescaped.items())\n    return result\n","numLines":247,"startLine":1,"totalLines":247}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01QmpF2sDUgXLNVSnxxxa3dY","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Aha! There's the bug! In a regex character class, the dash `-` at the end has special meaning - it denotes a range. When it's at the end of the character class like `[\"-+?~^/\\\\,]`, it's treated as a literal dash, not as a range operator. But I think there might be an issue with how it's being interpreted.\n\nActually, wait. Let me re-examine this. In the pattern `[\\[\\]\\(\\)\\{\\}:\"-+?~^/\\\\,]`:\n- `[` and `]` are escaped\n- `(` and `)` are escaped\n- `{` and `}` are escaped\n- `:` is literal\n- `\"` is literal\n- `-` is... this is the problem. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_018QZ9jQHvmR1DyWQnXbYqc4","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Interesting! I see that:1. 'AND horror' and 'horror AND' are being handled correctly by the fallback to fully_escape_query\n2. But 'Horror-' is not being escaped\n\nThe issue is that 'Horror-' is valid Lucene syntax (it just means 'Horror' without the minus operator applied to anything), so it doesn't raise a ParseError in escape_unknown_fields. Then when luqum_parser is called, it also passes, so we never reach the fallback to fully_escape_query.\n\nSo the issue is that we need to escape special characters BEFORE trying to parse with escape_unknown_fields, not just in the fallback.\n\nLet me check what characters should be escaped. Looking at the test cases in the test file:\n- 'flatland:a romance of many dimensions' -> 'flatland\\\\:a romance of many dimensions'\n- This is handled by escape_unknown_fields since there's a colon that's not a valid field\n\nBut for edge cases like trailing dashes, we need additional escaping. Let me look at the process_user_query function again and see if there's a better place to add escaping.\n\nActually, looking at the current implementation, it seems like the code already tries to escape some special characters:\n```python\nq_param = escape_unknown_fields(            (                q_param.strip()\n                .replace('/', '\\\\/')\n                .replace('?', '\\\\?')\n                .replace('~', '\\\\~')\n            ),\n```\n\nSo it's already escaping `/`, `?`, and `~`. But it's not escaping the dash. Maybe we should add dashes to this list?\n\nBut wait, dashes can be valid in queries (like in range queries or as word separators), so we need to be careful. Let me think about this more carefully.\n\nActually, the issue is more subtle. Looking at Lucene documentation:- Dashes have special meaning only when used as the minus operator (unary prefix)\n\n\n- A trailing dash like in 'Horror-' passes validation because it's syntactically valid, even though Solr might interpret it unexpectedly. The problem is that both escape_unknown_fields and luqum_parser accept it without error, so the fully_escape_query fallback never triggers. The test expects 'Horror\\\\-' but we're getting 'Horror-' because the query bypasses the escaping logic entirely.\n\nI need to handle edge cases more aggressively—specifically detecting when dashes appear at word boundaries where they could confuse the parser. The issue mentions that trailing hyphens, operator-like tokens, and similar patterns cause misinterpretation in Solr. Rather than relying on validation errors to trigger escaping, I should proactively escape dashes in positions where they're likely to cause problems, like at the end of terms.\n\nLooking at the actual implementation, the `process_user_query` function already handles several escape cases: forward slashes (which could trigger regex mode), question marks, and tildes. It applies these transformations before passing the query to `escape_unknown_fields`. I should follow this same pattern for problematic dash positions—escape them as part of the initial cleanup step rather than trying to detect and fix them later. When Solr encounters a trailing dash, it either ignores it or raises an error since the operator has nothing to apply to. The current approach escapes dashes in `fully_escape_query`, so `Horror-` becomes `Horror\\-`, but this only happens when the initial parse fails. For syntactically valid queries like `Horror-`, we're not applying this escaping, which could still cause issues.\n\nI need to reconsider the strategy—pre-escaping dashes before validation might work, but risks breaking legitimate range queries or other dash-based syntax. Looking back at the test expectations to understand what behavior is actually If the tree\n    ends up being empty, errors.\n\n    :param child: Node to remove\n    :param parents: Path of parent nodes leading from the root of the tree\n    \"\"\"\n    parent = parents[-1] if parents else None\n    if parent is None:\n        # We cannot remove the element if it is the root of the tree\n        raise EmptyTreeError()\n    elif isinstance(parent, (BaseOperation, Group, Unary)):\n        new_children = tuple(c for c in parent.children if c != child)\n        if not new_children:\n            # If we have deleted all the children, we need to delete the parent\n            # as well. This caused parsing errors or incorrect query semantics for edge cases.\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe primary issue was in the `fully_escape_query` function in `/workspace/openlibrary/openlibrary/solr/query_utils.py`. The regex pattern used to escape special characters had a bug:\n\n- Original pattern: `r'[\\[\\]\\(\\)\\{\\}:\"-+?~^/\\\\,]'`\n- The dash (`-`) was being interpreted as a range operator (from `\"` ASCII 34 to `+` ASCII 43) instead of a literal dash character\n- This caused dashes to NOT be escaped, leading to Solr parsing errors for queries with trailing dashes\n\n### Changes Made\n\n**1. Let me create a comprehensive summary of the fixes I've implemented:\n\n## Summary\n\nI have successfully fixed the work search query processing issues for edge-case inputs in the Open Library repository. Here are the changes made:\n\n### Issues Fixed\n\nFollowing the introduction of the SearchScheme-based work search, raw user queries were not consistently normalized and escaped before reaching Solr. This caused parsing errors or incorrect query semantics for edge cases.\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe primary issue was in the `fully_escape_query` function in `/workspace/openlibrary/openlibrary/solr/query_utils.py`. The regex pattern used to escape special characters had a bug:\n\n- Original pattern: `r'[\\[\\]\\(\\)\\{\\}:\"-+?~^/\\\\,]'`\n- The dash (`-`) was being interpreted as a range operator (from `\"` ASCII 34 to `+` ASCII 43) instead of a literal dash character\n- This caused dashes to NOT be escaped, leading to Solr parsing errors for queries with trailing dashes\n\n### Changes Made\n\n**1. Fixed the regex pattern in `fully_escape_query` (query_utils.py line 126)**\n   - Changed: `r'[\\[\\]\\(\\)\\{\\}:\"-+?~^/\\\\,]'`\n   - To: `r'[\\[\\]\\(\\)\\{\\}:\"\\-+?~^/\\\\,\\']'`\n   - This properly escapes dashes (`\\-`) and adds single quote escaping (`\\'`)\n\n**2. Added doctest for single quote handling (query_utils.py line 121-122)**\n   - Added test case: `fully_escape_query(\"foo's bar\")` → `\"foo\\\\'s bar\"`\n   - Ensures single quotes in queries are properly escaped\n\n**3.
